    <form n="infl">       
                     <orth orig="Ba" lang="ar">طَعَمَ</orth>
                  </form>, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">طَعْمٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">طَعَامٌ</foreign>, <hi rend="ital">He ate it;</hi> namely, food: (K, * TA:) and <foreign lang="ar">طَعِمَ</foreign>, aor. as above, inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">طُعْمٌ</foreign>, with damm, <hi rend="ital">he tasted</hi> [a thing]: (K:) or <foreign lang="ar">طَعِمَ</foreign>, aor. as above, (S, Mgh, * Msb,) inf. n. <foreign lang="ar">طُعْمٌ</foreign>, with damm, (S,) or <foreign lang="ar">طَعْمٌ</foreign>, with fet-h, (Msb,) or both, (Mgh,) and <foreign lang="ar">مَطْعَمٌ</foreign> also is an inf. n. of the same verb, (TA,) signifies <hi rend="ital">he ate,</hi> (S, Mgh, Msb, *) a thing, (Mgh,) and [app. also <hi rend="ital">he swallowed,</hi> for it is said that] it applies to anything that is swallowed easily or agreeably, even to water: (Msb:) and <hi rend="ital">he tasted</hi> (S, Mgh, Msb) a thing; (Mgh, Msb;) as also   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n26726-1" target="تطعّم" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n26726"/></foreign>; (S, Mgh, K;) [i. e.] this latter verb signifies <hi rend="ital">he tasted</hi> food <hi rend="ital">in order that he might know its flavour;</hi> and so   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n26726-2" target="استطعم" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign>: (Msb:) and <foreign lang="ar">طَعِمَ</foreign> as meaning <hi rend="ital">he tasted</hi> may be used in relation to that which is eaten and to that which is drunk. (L.) Hence, in the Kur [xxxiii. 53], <foreign lang="ar">فَإِذَا طَعِمْتُمْ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">فَٱنْتَشِرُوا</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">And when ye shall have eaten</hi> [<hi rend="ital">disperse yourselves</hi>]. (S, * TA.) And you say, <foreign lang="ar">فُلَانٌ قَلَّ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">طُعْمُهُ</foreign>, meaning [<hi rend="ital">Such a one,</hi>] <hi rend="ital">his eating</hi> [<hi rend="ital">was,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">became, little</hi>]. (S.) The saying in the Kur [ii. 250], <foreign lang="ar">وَمَنْ لَمْ يَطْعَمْهُ فَإِنَّهُ مِنِّى</foreign> means <hi rend="ital">But whoso does not taste it,</hi> (S, Msb, * TA,) <hi rend="ital">he is of my followers,</hi> (Bd, Jel,) or <hi rend="ital">is at one,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in union, with me:</hi> (Bd:) or, accord. to Zj, the meaning is, <foreign lang="ar">لَمْ <ref cref="n26726-3" target="يَتَطَعَّمْ" n="3" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>بِهِ</foreign> [app. meaning <hi rend="ital">does not refresh himself with it as though with food</hi>]: (TA:) or, as some say, the passage in which it occurs denotes a prohibition to take aught save as much as is laded out with the hand; and when water has with it something that is chewed, one says of it <foreign lang="ar">يُطْعَمُ</foreign>. (Er-Rághib, TA.) <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n26726-4" target="تَطَعَّمْ" n="4" type="5" subtype="FSO" lang="ar"/>تَطْعَمْ</foreign> i. e. <hi rend="ital">Taste thou,</hi> (S, Mgh, K,) <hi rend="ital">then thou wilt have desire,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">appetence,</hi> (Mgh,) or <hi rend="ital">so that thou mayest have desire,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">appetence, and mayest eat;</hi> (S, K;) or <hi rend="ital">taste thou the food, for it will induce thee to eat it;</hi> (IB, TA;) is a prov., (IB, Mgh, TA,) said to him who refrains from an affair; meaning, commence it, for thy doing so will invite thee to finish it. (IB, TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">الطَّعْمُ</foreign> signifies also <hi rend="ital">The eating with the central incisors:</hi> one says, <foreign lang="ar">إِنَّهُ لَيَطْعَمُ طَعْمًا حَسَنًا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Verily he eats well with the central incisors</hi>]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  And <foreign lang="ar">المُطْعِمَةُ</foreign>, (K, TA,) or, as written by Z, with fet-h, [i. e.
